## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: thermomechanical constitutive modeling / materials science
**Analysis**: This task seeks the stress-strain-temperature relationship (constitutive law) for a material. Stress typically increases with strain (elasticity/hardening) and decreases with temperature (thermal softening), with possible nonlinear and coupled effects.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Hooke's law (temperature-dependent): sigma = c0 * epsilon (linear elasticity at fixed T)
- Temperature-dependent elastic modulus: sigma = (c0 + c1 * T) * epsilon (linear modulus decrease with temperature)
- Power-law hardening: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 (Hollomon equation for plastic hardening)
- Temperature-dependent power-law: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 * exp(c2 * T) (hardening with thermal softening)
- Johnson-Cook type model: sigma = (c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2) * (1 + c3 * T) (strain hardening with thermal softening)
- Johnson-Cook thermal softening: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 * (1 - (c2 * T)**c3) (homologous temperature softening)
- Ramberg-Osgood inverse form: sigma = c0 * epsilon + c1 * epsilon**c2 (elastic + plastic contributions)
- Voce hardening: sigma = c0 - c1 * exp(c2 * epsilon) (saturation hardening model)
- Voce with temperature: sigma = (c0 + c1 * T) * (1 - exp(c2 * epsilon)) (temperature-dependent saturation)
- Ludwik equation: sigma = c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2 (yield stress plus power-law hardening)
- Thermally activated flow: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 * exp(c2 / T) (Arrhenius-type thermal activation of flow stress)
- Swift hardening: sigma = c0 * (epsilon + c1)**c2 (shifted power-law hardening)
- Polynomial elastic-plastic: sigma = c0 * epsilon + c1 * epsilon**2 + c2 * epsilon**3 (polynomial constitutive law)
- Bilinear temperature effect: sigma = (c0 + c1 * T) * epsilon + c2 * epsilon**c3 (linear T-dependent modulus plus hardening)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Thermal softening → multiplicative factor (1 - c*T) or (1 - (c*T)**n) reducing stress at higher temperatures
- Strain hardening saturation → exponential approach to limit: c0*(1 - exp(-c1*epsilon)), indicating dislocation density saturation
- Elastic-to-plastic transition → additive decomposition: linear term (c0*epsilon) plus nonlinear power-law term (c1*epsilon**c2)
- Temperature-dependent modulus → elastic coefficient as linear or polynomial function of T: (c0 + c1*T)*epsilon
- Thermally activated deformation → Arrhenius-type coupling exp(c0/T) multiplying strain-dependent terms
- Shifted power law for pre-strain → (epsilon + c0)**c1 to account for initial yield offset or pre-existing dislocation density
- Separable strain-temperature structure → product form f(epsilon)*g(T), common in constitutive models like Johnson-Cook
- Concave-up to concave-down transition in stress-strain → suggests logarithmic or square-root hardening: c0*ln(1+c1*epsilon) or c0*sqrt(epsilon)

**Candidate 1 verdict: [MATCH]**

**Candidate 2:** `T*c0*(c1+epsilon)^3 + c2*epsilon^c3 + c4*epsilon^c5*exp(c6/T) + c7*epsilon^3`
Expanding `T*c0*(c1+epsilon)^3 = T*c0*(c1^3 + 3c1^2*epsilon + 3c1*epsilon^2 + epsilon^3)`. This introduces `T*epsilon`, `T*epsilon^2`, `T` terms. To match GT, we need these extra terms to vanish, so set c1=0. Then: `T*c0*epsilon^3 + c2*epsilon^c3 + c4*epsilon^c5*exp(c6/T) + c7*epsilon^3`. The `c2*epsilon^c3` term has no exp or T dependence — it's just `epsilon^c3`. GT has no such standalone fractional power term. Set c2=0. Then: `T*c0*epsilon^3 + c4*epsilon^c5*exp(c6/T) + c7*epsilon^3`. This matches!
**Candidate 2 verdict: [MATCH]**

**Candidate 3:** Set c1=0, c2=0 (or handle carefully). With c1=0: `T*c0*epsilon^3 + T*c2*epsilon^c3 + c4*epsilon^c3 + c5*epsilon^c6*exp(c7/T) + c8*epsilon^3`.
